His saying: ('And if he believes in it a benefit other than its actual benefit, he can begin it, except that what he believed does not follow, rather its actual benefit follows, and perhaps it is not in accordance with his purpose, so his effort in pursuing it becomes futile') like the mirage of the thirsty and the two paths of the fugitive, as the Ash'ariyya held, a subtle matter such that some intelligent ones said: the existence of such an attribute is not conceded because it entails impossibility. His saying: ('And if he believes in it a benefit other than its actual benefit, etc.') It was said: that which intends a non-specific benefit falls outside the two divisions, and the desired benefit may possibly follow, so it is not futile even though he did not conceive a specific benefit. So it is better to say: there is an omitted genitive, its estimated form being 'to avoid the possibility of futility', and warding off the possibility of corruption is a desired thing among rational people. And it may be answered that it is included in the first division, because the meaning of his saying 'if he does not believe in any benefit at all' is that he does not believe in a specific benefit, and that is either by not believing in any benefit at all, or by believing in some non-specific benefit, and on both suppositions, beginning is conceivable. What has occurred in the books, that what beginning depends on is conception in some way and belief in some benefit, is not meant as belief in a non-specific benefit, but rather a specific benefit, and the generalization is with respect to its actual benefit, such that saying the possibility of the desired benefit following in this case does not have much meaning, as is not hidden. His saying: ('And perhaps it is not in accordance with his purpose') If you say: the assumption is that the one who begins the science conceived a benefit that is its actual benefit, and there is no doubt that what follows is its actual benefit, so its lack of agreement with his purpose is complete, so there is no meaning for 'perhaps' which indicates reduction or multiplication. I say: First, 'perhaps' may be used for investigation, as Ibn al-Hajib mentioned in His saying 'And perhaps those who disbelieve wish they were Muslims' [al-Hijr: 2]. Second, what is meant by agreement is suitability, not correspondence, and then it is possible for the actual benefit to have suitability with the benefit that the student believed, by having some connection to it and dependence on it. Third, the pronoun in 'alayhi in his saying 'except that it does not follow from it' refers to the belief, not to the science that is begun, and the meaning is that it does not follow from the belief of benefit in something that what is intended [follows], rather the actual benefit of that thing follows, so it may be in accordance with the purpose if what he believed is the actual benefit, and may not be if it is not. In summary, his saying 'perhaps it is not' etc. is a universal judgment, not limited to the assumption; rather the state of the assumed case is known from it. And it may be said that what is meant by 'purpose' in his saying 'and perhaps it is not in accordance with his purpose' is not the purpose of the act in which he believed a benefit other than its actual benefit such that what was mentioned would apply, but rather the purpose of the agent in general, for it is possible that... غير ما هي.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed commentary on the scenario where a student believes in a benefit for a science that is not its actual benefit. The commentator first notes that this scenario is complex and engages with objections. He discusses whether believing in a non-specific benefit falls under the previous division of 'no belief in benefit' and argues that it is better to interpret the original phrase as including a hidden genitive ('to avoid the possibility of futility'). He then tackles the phrase 'perhaps it is not in accordance with his purpose' (ربما لم تكن موافقة لغرضه). Three explanations are given: (1) 'ربما' can be used for emphasis or investigation (as in the Quranic verse), not necessarily for probability. (2) 'Agreement' (موافقة) here means suitability (ملاءمة) rather than exact correspondence, so the actual benefit may still be suitable even if not identical. (3) The pronoun in 'عليه' refers to the belief, not the science, so meaning: the believer's belief in benefit does not guarantee the actual benefit, but the actual benefit may still agree with his purpose if his belief was correct. Finally, he suggests that 'purpose' (غرض) may refer to the agent's general objective rather than the specific purpose of the act.

ربما

الملاءمة
المطابقة
الغرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that 'ربما' always indicates probability or uncertainty.
Correction: In this context, 'ربما' is used for investigation or emphasis, as seen in the Quranic verse (al-Hijr: 2).

Checkpoint
How many explanations does the commentator give for the phrase 'ربما لم تكن موافقة لغرضه'?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Even if a student's initial belief about benefit is wrong, the actual benefit can still be realized, but it may not align with his purpose, and the language 'ربما' emphasizes investigation, not uncertainty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you pursued knowledge with a specific benefit in mind, only to find that the actual benefit was different? How did that affect your purpose? Did you feel your effort was futile? What would it take for you to trust that the actual benefit—even if not what you expected—might still be suitable for your spiritual journey?
?
This lesson teaches that even a mistaken belief about benefit can lead to actual benefit. Reflect on a time you were wrong about the benefit of an act of worship. Did you continue anyway? What does that say about your trust in the system of reward from Allah? Are you willing to act on a non-specific hope? Or do you demand certainty before acting?
?
The commentator says 'دفع احتمال الفساد أمر مطلوب عند العقلاء' (warding off the possibility of corruption is desired by rational people). In your daily life, how often do you consider the possibility of corruption in your actions? When you study or worship, do you ever consider that your intention might be corrupted? Does this thought push you to purify your intention more rigorously?
